This is my favorite recipe that I have found at allrecipes.com - I fell in love with it when I was making (and tasting) the sauce! The sauce is AMAZING and so delicious, really to die for, and it *makes* the dish. The sauce is the perfect combination of sweet and salty, aromatic and delightful. I make this in huge batches and I add cherry tomatoes, blanched snap peas, baby carrots, and celery. We eat it as the main course, and we have yummy leftovers for the day after. I have made this recipe over and over again.

text:
I've received many compliments on this recipe, having served it a few times.  I would only alter a few things:  add julienned carrots, sliced water chestnuts and pea pods cut in half on an angle- really adds nice color, texture and flavor.  Knock oil down to 1/3 cup otherwise it is REALLY oily.  I use fettucine noddles.  If you are making this ahead and chilling it (which I would recommend), add half of the dressing while noodles are still warm and will soak up flavor. MMM! Toss the other half of the dressing before serving.  I like it warm OR cold, but feel it is better cold.  Still great the next day.  Will make again and again!!

text:
liked the flavor of this and am a huge fan of cilantro, but this is deffinately a dish I would leave it out!  The green onions with the sesame sauce is perfect.  You're in better luck when using chunks of chicken, shredded makes the salad a little messy.  You can eat this hot or cold its great!

second review-  this recipe gets better and better as you make it!  I'm eating low carb so today I made this (still left the cilantro out) with low carb linguini (snapped them in half so they are short noodles) made the sauce with olive oil instead of vegetable oil, used splenda instead of regular sugar and added vegetables to the green onion like some bok choy, whole canned mushrooms, sugar snap peas, water chestnuts and julianned carrots.  INCREDIBLE!!  I love this stuff hot and cold.  I usually bring a container to work and tend to eat it hot, but by the time its lunch and I'm ready to do that, its gone!  great meal and great dish to bring to a party.

This is a great basic recipe which you can tweak for your own tastes. Took the advice of some reviewers and reduced the oil (evoo) and added a little chili oil for a kick. Also added a clove of garlic.  Poured some of the dressing on warm noodles; also marinated some chicken breasts in the dressing before cooking. Finally, took fresh snow peas and put them in the bottom of a colander, then poured cooked pasta over them to blanch them. Finished up by adding some red bell pepper for flavor and color. Really enjoyed the result.

text:
Excellent! I toasted the sesame seeds, lightly, then set it aside. I reduced the oil to 1/3 cup (3T) and the sugar to 1 1/2 Tablespoons. I think that 3T sugar would make the dressing too sweet. I also added fresh grated ginger to the dressing. I poured half of the dressing over the cooked spiral pasta to let the it absorb the flavors. I placed the the pasta and other half of salad dressing in the refrigerator until ready to serve. I had some leftover rotisserie chicken so I chopped that up. This salad is versatile and can be adjusted to other vegetables. For color, flavor and texture, I added sugar snap peas (par boiled), cherry tomatoes, halved, and carrots, julienned.  I poured the remainder of the dressing over the pasta along with the chicken and vegetables then tossed to coat evenly. I garnished the pasta salad with chopped green onions and cilantro. To me the salad dressing is the star -very light yet flavorful with an "Asian" flair! The dressing is not too sweet or oily. Everything is seasoned perfectly with a subtle sweetness, little "tang" and fresh flavors. I loved the crunch of the sugar snap peas and carrots. The cherry tomatoes are naturally sweet and brightens up the pasta as well. The cilantro adds a lovely flavor. This salad is appealing, delicious and satisfying! It is perfect for a hot and humid day like today in Hawaii! I also served, "Bruce's Honey Sesame Bread, " also from this website.

text:
Who knew that you could make such an awesome Asian pasta salad at home?!?!  After reading the "most helpful" reviews, I decided to make a few changes.  First, decrease the oil to 1/3 cup.  Someone recommended to omit the cilantro & I think that would be a BIG mistake.  This dish screams for some freshness, and the cilantro is perfect.  I felt that it really needed some veggies, so I added some shredded carrots, sliced cucumber (halved & seeded), and blanched snow peas.  Each of them add great crunch.  I cut the snow peas and green onion on a diagonal for some flare.  I thought it was strange that the recipe called for bow tie pasta.  Lo Mein noodles seemed like the most natural and perfect fit to me.  You can find them in the Asian isle at your supermarket.  That was definitely the most important change to make it feel authentic.  I also made it easy on myself by purchasing an already cooked rotisserie chicken from the grocery store & cubing the meat.  I just made it and can already tell that it will be even better when it has a chance to cool down.  Make it with the above changes and you will NOT be disappointed!!!

text:
I thought the flavor was fine, but as other reviewers suggested, the addition of snow peas, water chestnuts, etc. would definitely help out an otherwise pretty plain looking pasta salad.  The problem I had with it that no one else commented on is that because the dressing is a liquid base and not creamy, it doesn't stick to the pasta at all.  When I was done mixing it, the dressing immediately just kind of sank to the bottom of the bowl.  I think the recipe is certainly worth playing around with; I think I'll trying heating the dressing ingredients on the stove and add just a bit of cornstarch to thicken it up so that it stays on the bow tie pasta. I'm giving some to my husband in his lunch tomorrow for work, and I've already warned him to make sure he stirs it before he eats it, because all the dressing will be in the bottom of the container.

I know some hate when a review is posted and you change the recipe, but this was such a good starting point, I think it deserves a 5.  What I did differently:  used about a 1/4 cup sesame oil, low-sodium tamari sauce, fresh ginger juice, and agave nectar in the dressing.  And for the veggies:  sliced green onions, thinly-sliced yellow and red pepper, shaved carrots, and edamame.  I also used black toasted sesame seeds.  It's a beautiful and very tasty dish.  I made for lunch and ate warm.  Now it's going in the fridge for tomorrow's lunch cold and we'll see which way I prefer it.  Oh, I also omitted the cilantro--can't stand the stuff.  : )

The first time I made this, I followed the directions exactly and thought it was pretty plain.  I wasn't going to ever make it again, but I had to make dinner on the fly and thought I would give this another chance, with modifications.  This recipe is definitely not 5 stars on its own.  Many reviewers added veggies because it just falls flat when made as is.  I added shredded carrots, chopped green onions, sweet peas, and crushed roasted peanuts.  I also seasoned the chicken with onion powder, garlic powder, salt, and fresh ground peppercorn melange before cooking, and I added garlic powder and red pepper flakes to the sauce.  More seasonings and vegetables make this much more pleasing to the palate.

text:
Great recipe! I really loved the flavours,  so did my husband. My 5 year old was not a fan though. I knew it would be a gamble with him given the strong flavour of sesame oil. But you never know unless you present different things! For hubby and I, I added chili pepper flakes to offset the sweetness. I also added some julienned bell peppers for flavour and crunch. We had some leftover grilled chicken to use up so this recipe was handy. It's quick, tasty, and simple to make. To ensure the dressing doesn't sit on the bottom, don't rinse the pasta. Put the dressing on while the noodles are still warm, then refrigerate the pasta salad for at least 2 hours, stirring after 1 hour. It coats well and distributes evenly. I used the conversion on All Recipes to half the recipe; it was perfect for 4 servings and there's enough left over for one lunch. This dish is good cold and warm. I could hardly stay out of it before putting it in the fridge to chill!

text:
This was great!  I think it would taste excellent with tofu as a vegetarian alternative (just make sure you wrap up the tofu in a towel, put it between two dishes, with something heavy on top, to drain out excess water).   Minor changes-  I sauteed the chicken with garlic powder, onion powder, and black pepper.  I added extra garlic powder and onion powder to the salad later (I felt they added good extra flavor). I lowered the sugar in half (just trying to make it more healthy, didn't miss the extra sugar at all....  ).  Added the sesame seeds in raw/plain (in other words, did not need to use the vegetable oil to toast them....   again, did not miss the extra oil/toasting).  I'll make this one again-  it was tasty and with modifications, pretty healthy!   Also wanted to add, i feel the oil is too much---- i feel halving the vegetable oil would be wise.  Hence why i give this one a 4/5.  if the oil had been closer to par, i would've given it a 5.  And yes, i will gladly make it again!

I just made this tonight along with Firecracker Grilled Alaska Salmon; both had an Asian flavor I was craving.  This recipe is very forgiving, and thus will become a staple in my collection!  I omitted the cilantro and green onions (didn't have on hand), used fresh ginger, and traded olive oil for the veggie oil (eyeballed amount), per another reviewer's suggestion. I also subbed some of the rice vinegar with yummy white wine.  Since I used grilled salmon infused with it's own flavor, I could see why you'd need to season the chicken before adding it to the pasta. Overall, delicious! Just add more salt, fresh ginger, or sesame seeds to your liking. Thanks for a healthier pasta recipe!

The first time I made this I followed the recipe exactly.  It was okay but much too oily and it needed some vegetables.

The second time I made this I used whole wheat pasta, cut the vegetable oil down to an 1/8 of a cup but added a few dashes of hot chili oil. I used a whole chicken instead of just breast meat and left out the cilantro because it didn't do it for me the first time around.

I think most of the changes were for the best.  The whole wheat pasta had a less than ideal texture cold but it was good hot.

Overall, I liked this, however I only used about 2/3 of the amount of pasta called for, and I increased the chicken to 4 cups, otherwise it would have been more pasta than anything. I didn't have sesame oil so I didn't use it. It may have helped give it more flavor had I used it. It wasn't bland, but it didn't have as much taste as I'd have liked. I made it a day in advance, so before serving it, I mixed in a little more rice wine vinegar (would have added a little more soy sauce too, but I was out), and I toasted some sliced almonds to sprinkle on top to give it some crunch since the sesame seeds were a little soggy by the next day. In general though, it was good...everyone liked it.

text:
This is a great recipe and has been added to our monthly recipe rotation.  Very versatile depending on ingredients on hand.  As others have said reduce oil to 1/3.  Also, only use half the dressing when first mixing together.    For those of you not using the sesame oil or poppy seeds it does make a big difference.  If too expensive look in the Mexican and Chinese sections of your grocery store.  Both items will be there at reduced rates.  (Ex: sesame oil in regular oil section is $7.99, but in the Chinese section a slightly smaller bottle is only $2.99 - a little goes a long way so get the smaller bottle)

The taste was exactly what I was hoping for when I came across this recipe.  It was fabulous!  I made this to take along in a cooler for tailgating and it went over well.  I have two more tailgating ventures in the next couple months so I will be making this again!

I flavored 4 chicken breasts with soy sauce, garlic powder and lemon pepper and cooked them in a skillet.  I reduced the vegetable oil to 1/4 cup - I think if I had used the entire 1/2 cup it probably would have been too oily.  I also added julienned carrots for color and texture.

This one is a keeper!

text:
"Sesame Pasta Chicken Salad" is quite delicious. I made mine with gluten-free pasta. After tasting the dressing, I did need to modify it to punch it up for our well-seasoned international palates (2 tablespoons of siracha, 2 cloves of garlic, 1 teaspoon of fresh grated ginger). I used gluten-free tamari in place of the soy sauce. I also used toasted sesame oil for half of the vegetable oil in the dressing, and it did not have an overwhelming sesame flavor. Plain sesame oil is almost flavorless, so you do not get an Asian flavor. I did not add sugar because we do not like sweet food in our family. I wanted to serve this salad as a main course, but felt like it was "missing vegetables," which meant I had to make a special trip to the store for cherry tomatoes and snow peas. I loved this salad in concept, and am highly likely to make a modified version of it again because it is such a fast-and-easy make-ahead meal. Thank you ohines for sharing your recipe.

text:
LOVED this recipe!  Took it to a potluck dinner and the bowl was EMPTY.  Everyone asked me for the recipe!  Luckily I saved a portion for myself for lunch today, and it was great even 2 days after preparation.

I made a few changes, based on reading the reviews (and I'm glad I did - the dish was DELICIOUS!)

I reduced the oil to 1/3 cup and I used peanut oil.  I also added 1/2 teaspoon of garlic salt, 2 tablespoons of fresh lime juice, and red pepper flakes for a little kick.  I stirred in a finely chopped red pepper for crunch and flavor.  I also took the recommendation to use half the dressing on the pasta the night of preparation, and then stire in the other half right before serving.  I gave the pasta one last squeeze of fresh lime juice right before serving - really brightened it up.  I didn't use any cilantro because I hate the stuff.

Amazing results! Tangy, sweet/sour, great flavors.  I will definitely be making this one again!

One of my new favorite recipes! It was a bit boring, so I added a ton of veggies to it. Bean sprouts, snap peas, zucchini, squash, shredded carrotts a green onion. After I cook the chicken, I add a little extra oil and sautee the veggies. Keeping some crunch on them. I also do not do the sugar, but add 1 packet of Splenda to the "sauce". The sauce totally makes this recipe and I usually add a bit more soy and rice wine to the mix. SO GOOD! I like to add a sprinkle of red hot chili flakes before serving. I have made this several times in the last couple of months. Make a big batch and eat off of it several times.

I used 5 med.-size boneless, skinless chicken thighs, seasoned with seasoned salt, garlic powder and pepper then microwaved about 10 minutes. I cut the oil in half after reading reviews, and I added blanched and chilled sugar snap peas (boiled for 1 min. then plunged in ice water for several minutes - this gives the peas a bright green color but they remain nice and crunchy) Also added an 11 oz. can of mandarin oranges drained and cut in half (would have added another can but only had one).  This was insanely delicious!

The first time, it marinated for about 6 hours and this time I didn't let it sit and marinate at all. Still so good! I'll be making this one again and again.

text:
This stuff is so good!  I was asked to bring a side dish to a party and brought this and it was a big hit.  I altered the dressing a bit based on another recipe on this site "Asian Chicken Salad".  It's very similar but makes less dressing and uses brown sugar instead of white.  I think as written this would be far too much dressing for one box of bow tie pasta.  I would scale it in half.  I also added shredded carrot for color and I used a can of chicken breast meat instead of cooking the chicken which saves a ton of time.  I drained the chicken and placed it in a bowl, added a bit of the dressing to it then added it to the pasta.  It was a great light and tasty side dish.

text:
My family loved this recipe!  I followed some reviewers suggestions and added a half a bag of diagonally sliced snow peas and two thirds cup shredded carrots during the last minute of the pasta boil time, drained it all together, and added half the dressing while the pasta was still slightly warm, adding the remaining dressing with the rest of the ingredients. I also reduced the vegetable oil to 1/4 cup and increased the sesame oil to 2 tablespoons. I added extra green onions for crunch and flavor and topped with the juice of half a lime. Lastly, for extra flavor, we pre-marinated the chicken in a bottled Island teriyaki sauce and grilled it before we cooled and chopped it and added it to the salad. Delicious dish!

Love this recipe and use all kinds of variations to it - I use it to clean out the veggies I have left over, red peppers cut into matchsticks, peas, cauliflower, mushrooms, etc.  I do cut the vegetable oil down to 1/4 - 1/3 cup and up the sesame oil to 1 tablespoon. text:
OH MY GOD... this recipe is my lord and savior! It's so easy and tastes amazing every time. I like to make it after work because it doesn't feel too daunting to prepare after a long busy day.

I make this exactly as it's written with a few minor adjustments to make it more vegetarian:
- Omit the chicken
- I cut up a medium-large head of broccoli
- I julienne a carrot
- I cut up 1 red pepper
- I add PEANUT BUTTER

While the pasta cooks I stir-fry all the veggies, and when they're close to being done I add the sauce and let it simmer on low-medium. My secret ingredient is 1 heaping tablespoon of peanut butter! I add the peanut butter while it the sauce simmers with the veggies. It literally takes the recipe NEXT LEVEL!

I also like to squirt that good, good Sriracha into the sauce. I also crack a ton of pepper into it. 

IT'S SO EFFING GOOD!!! You must try. 
OBEY YOUR CRAVINGS!

text:
I love this recipe, but I made several alterations to it. I added only about half the amount of vegetable oil and rice vinegar, and instead of using basic soy sauce I used Ponzu (soy sauce with a citrus flavor - there are a few kinds but I prefer the orange one with a little bit of lime) as well as Hoisin (which is like an Asian bbq sauce). I just add these to taste as I mix a little at a time into the salad. It may sound like an odd combination but it is really very good. I also added a little of each of the sauces to the chicken when cooking it. I also added red, yellow and orange bell peppers. The last time I made it I also just left out the ginger, I prefer the flavor of the sauces and having all that flavor all at once is too much, in my opinion. 

I have brought this to several parties in place of a basic pasta salad and everyone LOVES it! It is a great dish if you want something unique that is still not too "different" that it would scare people off.

text:
this was really good. i made it a little different, i reduced the oil to 1/3. i cooked chunks of chicken breast by sauting onion, garlic, ginger, one green hot pepper, mrs.dash, basil, oregano, onion powder and salt and pepper (all spices i have in my cabinet). after the pasta was cooked and strained i spooned the browned chicken in the hot steaming pasta and added a few tablespoons of the sauce i had prepared. i then sauteed finely chopped red peppers, carrots, corn, and green peas in the same pan. while the veggies were cooking i spooned some of the prepared sauce. finally when the veggies were cooked i mixed everything together and topped it with minced scallion and chopped cilantro. the cilantro gives it a lovely taste...it is very "wet" dish. i imagine when its cooled and refridgerated it will lose some liquid...it is definitely a side dish though. i just made a big pan of it and now i realize its nice to complement a main dish. not really a main course.

text:
Very good.  I made it exactly as the recipe instructed except that I reduced the oil to 1/3 cup since so many reviewers recommended that.  I felt like there wasn't enough dressing when I was ready to serve it, so I whipped up another batch of the dressing and added half of it to the salad.  I would caution you about toasting the sesame seeds.  I felt like medium high heat was too high, at least on my gas range.  Even though I stirred constantly, the seeds almost burned.  I would recommend medium heat at the most...maybe even medium low.  This is a good salad, and I plan to make it again.  With the extra dressing, this salad would probably be a 5 star.

text:
Fantastic recipe! It will surprise you by how good it is and how easy it is to make. I made a few changes, but am confident it would be just as yummy without them. I used regular soy sauce, cut the oil in half, added diced red pepper, used seasoned rice vinegar, and used some chopped chicken breasts that I had previously marinaded overnight in a sesame marinade and then grilled. I used a tiny bit more sesame oil than it called for... maybe 1/2 teaspoon more. This was so good, we finished it in four (healthy) servings... not ten. I brought the last bowl of it to work for lunch and my coworkers raved about it. The crispy LaChoy rice noodles sprinkled on top of broccoli florets mixed in would be nice additions. Oh, and I let it rest for about 15 minutes after mixing the dressing with the other ingredients to let the pasta soak up the sauce and let the flavors meld. It was DEE-LISH.

text:
This turned out pretty darn good! I had to make some modifications just based on what I had in the house. I used a box of spaghetti, omitted the cilantro and used toasted sliced almonds instead of sesame seeds. Like others, I added matchstick carrots, sliced cucumbers and tripled the green onions. I made the dressing according to the directions (only used 1/3 cup oil), but found it to be less than flavorful. So to jazz it up a little, I added a tbsp. of Sriracha, a couple tbsp. of creamy peanut butter and probably 4 tbsp. of Mae Ploy sweet chili sauce. That made it just about perfect! Taking it picnicking tomorrow; can't wait to try it really cold from the fridge!

text:
This is good! I wasn't blown away, but my husband, mother-in-law, and 2 year old all had seconds! I reduced the oil and was glad I did - the amount in the recipe was FAR too much. I did love the sesame oil and the Asian flavor it lent to the dish. Although I LOVE cilantro, I was disappointed by its weak contribution (even though I increased the amount). It seemed to be overpowered by the sesame and soy flavors. We all agreed that the addition of water chestnuts and mandarin oranges would greatly improve it. I would also perhaps reduce the sugar to 2 T. I will make this again, but with these changes.

This recipe is Great! I made it yesterday for a bbq/birthday party! I read several reviews before making the recipe. I cut back to 1/3 c of oil (which most people suggested),  I added red bell pepper, broccoli florest, sugar snap peas, shredded carrots, and slivered almonds! I also made two batches of the dressing. I poured 1/2 of the dressing on a few hours before serving and then the other half upon serving. Adding extra ingredients made the pasta so colorful and extra YUMMY! I also marinated my chicken in Seseme ginger marinade and cooked it on the grill! This pasta was a major hit! I think Ill add water chestnuts and mushroom next time! Multiple people asked for the recipe! Enjoy :)

text:
I only had spaghetti noodles so I used those instead of the bow ties. I cut the meat down to two cups and added one cup of steamed chopped broccoli. I didn't realize that I was out of sesame seeds until I went to grab them and they were gone, so I used 1/4 cup of chopped dry roasted peanuts. I also increased the ginger to a full teaspoon and used four cloves chopped fresh garlic in the "sauce". I took a small taste and thought it was great, and two boys out of my three liked it. I'll make this again. NOTE: I did serve this salad chilled. I think that by doing that, it made the salad even better.

text:
I do not write reviews often, but this recipe is amazing . For those that complain it turns brown, of course, there is soy sauce in it. Like others I doubled the dressing ingredients, except the oil, kept it at 1/3 cup. Next time I might not fully double the sesame seeds for the dressing as I found I had quite a bit. Put half on now and will re-toss later before I serve it at the party. A little note: it needs the green onion and cilantro, dont bother without them. I added blanched snow peas (threw them in the water with the pasta) and carrots. Yummy! UPDATE: I doubled the sauce, however, its not necessary. With the dressing I had I was able to make 2 batches and still had some left over. The second time around I put slightly more dressing and it wasn't as tasty. Don't go over board on it. But if you don't double the sauce ingredients, be sure to cut the oil in half.

text:
I didn't really care for this.  I make something really similar that we like a lot better.  I thought there was too much dressing, with too much soy sauce.  The version I make has 1/2 cup rice vinegar, 1/2 tsp dry mustard, 2 T honey, 2 T sugar, 1 T soy sauce, 2 T sesame oil, and 1/2 cup vegetable oil in the dressing.  I also put sliced water chestnuts in (I sprinkle some soy sauce over them and let them sit a little before adding them to the pasta).  I also add some peas.  My version has chicken in it as well.  And then we garnish each serving with some cilantro, chopped, peanuts (we don't use sesame seeds), and a squeeze of lime juice.  I'll stick to my version.  But, thanks for sharing the recipe.

text:
This was a very good pasta salad, though I did make some changes. Like other reviewers I only used a 1/4 cup oil and I scaled the sugar back just a bit. I added a large clove of garlic (minced), used fresh ginger (also minced) instead of dried, added about a cup of shelled edamame and a little less than that of sliced carrots. 

While I love spice, the rest of my family does not, but I bet this would be great with some hot chili flakes sprinkled in. I'll definitely make this again utilizing my changes and will experiment with other veggies (soybean or mung bean sprouts would probably be good, also broccoli or snap peas).

None
text:
I have been making a variation of this recipe for nearly 20 years. It is a nice, light and refreshing dish to serve at BBQs or potlucks. I always make it as a meatless side dish. 

I find that any shaped pasta is fine for this recipe. It doesn't really matter. I also have been adding diced green and red peppers, shredded and diced carrots, and peas (frozen or canned with no salt) for color and texture.

This recipe is best when made at least 4-6 hours in advance. I like to make it 24 hours in advance. It stores very nicely in the refrigerator. Just keep it sealed in a glass or plastic dish with lid. The day you are serving, just shake really well to combine ingredients.

I have been making this recipe since I found it over 2 years ago.I've made it for a big family get together,  for my immediate family,  for a group of people who are rough and tumble folks who rack up an appetite by the end of a long day riding modified jeeps through killer trails, drop offs, rocks, & you name it! They picked my salad over the other meals or snacks available! I arrived with two very large bowls, stuffed to the top and came home with nothing! I didn't change much. I sliced up snow peas into thinstrips-as I did with a red bell pepper. The thin strip offers brilliant color, crunch, & texture against the noodles and chicken, but not too much crunch. I slice the green onion on a bias at the very end, but mostly the white & crisper green parts. They not only add that little zing, but stay flavorful if you dish it out without mixing them in all throughout.  They tend to get mushy. I do not add cilantro, carrots,  peas, or any of the many other suggestions.  Let me tell you! This salad has more than enough flavor without adding much more! I actually had to make it from memory tonight because I just couldn't  find this recipe -I had it saved on another tablet that I cannot charge to even get to the saved recipes! I only put in the wrong amount of sugar in the dressing...that was all! Everyone should make this salad. Don't be afraid of it. It's absolutely delicious!  Thank you so much for putting it out there for me to find.

This is a huge hit for a "team meal"! Made many times for different groups, and everyone raved. 
I cut back the oil a bit. I use only about 2/3 of the dressing, so I reserve the toasted sesame seeds and toss them in later. (Since I want all of them in the salad). 
To cook the chicken breasts: Bring water to a boil ( I add in some teriaki if I have it) add chicken breasts with water to cover 1/2 inch over.  Return to boil, cover, remove from heat and let sit 15-20 minutes.

Loved it!!  I did it in the crock pot because it's super good to have in the summer and I don't want to stand over a hot stove for a long period of time.  I used a plastic bag crock pot liner and threw in everything except the noodles.  I also reduced the olive oil to about 1/3 C.  Cooked in the crock pot for about 5-6 hours on low, then shredded the chicken, put it back in the bag, and stuck the whole bag in the fridge until it was cool.  I boiled noodles on the stove, then rinsed them under cold water and added them to the bag as well for about 1/2 hour for the flavors to come together.  Everyone loved it.

I substituted the vegetable oil for coconut oil, and the sugar for an equal amount of agave syrup. Next time, I think I will only do 1.5-2 T of agave; 3 was a little too sweet. country:

text:
Loved this.  Alot. My husband, a great cook in his own right, is bad about not reading ahead and collecting ingredients so he started making this with no scallions/green onions, fresh ginger or fresh cilantro.  We made it with dried cilantro and dried gringer and left out the onions.  We were all out of sesame seeds to.  Oddly enough, it was good but with the right stuff could be phenomenal.  Do yourself a favor - do NOT omit the cilantro and use fresh, please use fresh ginger, the scallions would help.  Cut back on the oil, EVOO would be ok but the sesame oil is enough.  I'd use black and regular sesame seeds for appearance and go with the julienned carrots and angle-cut snap peas.  Bowtie pasta is fine but penne worked well to hold the dressing. Crushed cashews would be a great finshing touch.  Most importantly - either double batch it and eat some the day you make it but save the most for the following day or for *best* flavor - let it sit overnight!  All in all, we liked it enough that this was the first review I took the time to write.

text:
Meh. This was quite mediocre, IMHO. I wanted to make something quick for lunches this past week, but had little time available to cook over the weekend. This recipe seemed to fit the bill perfectly (and it certainly did!), but unfortunately, the end result was just so-so. For starters, once refrigerated, everything dried up (it's as if the sauce completely evaporated...). Additionally, eaten fresh, the flavors didn't have a chance to "meld" and the sesame taste was totally overwhelming. On day 2 (and now day 3), the flavor has improved, but my pasta is dry as a bone :( I scaled this recipe to 7 servings because I only had 2 cups worth of chicken (I purchased 2 (8 oz.) bags of oven roasted chicken strips on sale at my local grocer and cut them into tiny pieces - this was WAAAAY cheaper than purchasing a rotisserie chicken or a large "chunk" from my deli counter and much quicker than cubing/shredding myself). I wish I would have made the full 10 servings worth of dressing. I believe that would have taken care of the dryness issue, at least somewhat. Served with a ciabatta roll, this makes for a filling, yet light lunch. I just don't think I like this enough to add to my regular rotation. Thanks for sharing :)

I am thinking of carrots and broccoli and maybe a few almonds or cashews. My mouth is watering thinking about it. I definitely recommend using this recipe and making it your own way. It's delicious!

text:
Best pasta salad Ive ever made at home. I was on the hunt for a pasta salad to come close to an Asian-influenced one from a local deli that I adore, and while this one was different, it was equally yummy on its own merit!  Changes I made: I added a handful of julienned carrots, which i highly recommend for a nice crunch and it makes the salad MUCH prettier. I doubled the cilantro, because I personally love cilantro and thought the amount was too little, and for the chicken, i got a rotisserie chicken from my grocer and shredded that, which i think made it even more flavorful, since they generally inject those types of chicken with flavorings/juices.   This pasta salad was so dang good, it had me hunched over my Tupperware bin full of leftovers, gobbling it down whenever i could! definitely a new staple in my household diet!

text:
I used linguini noodles and sort of made it into a lo mein. I added mushrooms and bok choy and water chestnuts and an Asian medley from the frozen food section that had snap peas, broccoli, peppers, and baby corn. I added cilantro and green onions for garnish. I also made Traditional Potstickers found on this site and it was a great Asian theme night at my house! My hubby was so impressed! The sauce was great and pretty easy. I made the sauce first and kept it in the fridge while I made everything else and cooked the noodles al dente and sauced them as soon as they came out of the pot so they could soak up the sauce. The more the sauce sits the longer it develops because tasting it this morning right out of the fridge it was an explosion of flavor. Can't wait to eat the leftovers...what little is left!
